0056               ; Platforms supported:
0057               ; o TI-99/4A with 32k Memory Expansion
0058               
0059               ; this is intended to be assembled by xdt99, no console ROM dependencies
0060               ;   cvbasic --ti994a test1.bas test1.a99
0061               ;   xas99.py -R test1.a99
0062               
0063               ; When looking at this - remember that JUMP and BRANCH have the /opposite/
0064               ; meanings to the 6502 - JUMP is the short relative one, and BRANCH is absolute.
0065               
0066               ;
0067               ; CVBasic variables in scratchpad.
0068               ;
0069               
0070               ; don't warn on branch/jump optimizations or unused variables
0071               ;: warn-opts = off
0072               ;: warn-symbols = off
0073               
0074               ; use original (possibly incorrectly ported) random
0075      0000     OLD_RND equ 0
0076               
0077               ; We have to use our own workspace, not GPLWS, because the interrupt routine makes it unsafe to
0078               ; use r11, which we kind of need! So that eats 32 bytes of RAM but means most of the register
0079               ; restrictions I wrote this code on (avoid R1, avoid R6, avoid R13-R15) are lifted.
0080      8300     mywp      equ >8300
0081      8320     myintwp   equ >8320
0082               
0083               ; data storage in scratchpad
0084                   dorg >8340
0085               
0086               ; used to track scratchpad variables
0087      8340     firstsp         equ $
0088               
0089 8340          read_pointer    bss 2       ; for data/read statements
0090 8342          cursor		    bss 2       ; screen position
0091 8344          pletter_off	    bss 2       ; Used by Pletter
0092               
0093               ; joystick bytes
0094 8346          joy1_data	    bss 1       ; keep these bytes together and even aligned
0095 8347          joy2_data	    bss 1
0096               
0097 8348          key1_data	    bss 1       ; byte - keyboard - keep these bytes together and even aligned
0098 8349          key2_data	    bss 1       ; byte - keyboard (not used)
0099               
0100 834A          frame	        bss 2       ; word
0101 834C          lfsr		    bss 2       ; word MUST BE EVEN ALIGNED
0102               
0103 834E          mode            bss 1
0104 834F          flicker         bss 1
0105               
0106 8350          ntsc            bss 1

0148               
0154               
0155               ; used to track scratchpad variables
0156                   even
0157      8352     lastsp              equ $
0158               
0159               ; While we don't mean to USE the console ROM, for interrupts we
0160               ; are forced to interface with some of it. We need these addresses
0161               ; to minimize what it does so we can maximize our use of scratchpad.
0162               ; While I'd like to use the cassette hook - requires only 10 instructions
0163               ; and only uses 6 words of scratchpad, we can't here because it
0164               ; loses the return address, meaning you can only use it if you
0165               ; know where your LIMI 2 is and interrupts are otherwise disabled. So
0166               ; we have to use the longer but more standard interrupt hook, which also
0167               ; reads VDP status for us (no choice).
0168               
0169      8379     intcnt              equ >8379   ; interrupt counter byte, adds 1 (from GPLWS r14) every frame
0170      837B     vdp_status          equ >837B   ; VDP status byte mirror
0171      83C2     intwsr1             equ >83c2   ; INT WS R1  - interrupt control flags - must be >8000
0172      83C4     intwsr2             equ >83c4   ; INT WS R2  - address of user interrupt routine (point to int_handler)
0173      83D6     intwsr11            equ >83d6   ; screen timeout counter - must be odd (init to 1, is inct every frame)
0174      83DA     intwsr13            equ >83da   ; INT WS R13 - used for interrupt call (word)
0175      83DC     intwsr14            equ >83dc   ; INT WS R14 - used for interrupt call (word)
0176      83DE     intwsr15            equ >83de   ; INT WS R15 - used for interrupt call (word)
0177      83F6     gplwsr11            equ >83f6   ; GPL WS R11 - return address to interrupt ROM (not used, but overwritten each int)
0178      83F8     gplwsr12            equ >83f8   ; GPL WS R12 - used for cassette test and interrupt hook test (zeroed each int)
0179      83FA     gplwsr13            equ >83fa   ; GPL WS R13 - used in my interrupt handler
0180      83FC     gplwsr14            equ >83fc   ; GPL WS R14 - flags used to detect cassette - must be >0108 (or at least >0020 clear)
0181      83FE     gplwsr15            equ >83fe   ; GPL WS R15 - base address of VDP for status read - must be >8C02
0182               
0183               ; Some hardware equates
0184      83C0     INTWS     equ >83C0     ; interrupt calling Workspace
0185      83E0     GPLWP     equ >83E0     ; we use this one
0186      8400     SOUND     equ >8400
0187      8800     VDPDATA   equ >8800
0188      8802     VDPSTATUS equ >8802
0189      8C00     VDPWDATA  equ >8c00
0190      8C02     VDPWADR   equ >8c02

     6028 6000     
0205               
0206                   bank 0

0208 602A 0203  20     li r3,3         ; how many banks
     602C 0003     
0209 602E 0204  20     li r4,>6000     ; from bank
     6030 6000     
0210 6032 0200  20     li r0,>a000     ; target in RAM
     6034 A000     
0211               SFLP
0212 6036 04F4  30     clr *r4+        ; set the bank
0213 6038 0201  20     li r1,>6050     ; from address
     603A 6050     
0214 603C 0202  20     li r2,>1FB0     ; count
     603E 1FB0     
0215               SFLP2
0216 6040 CC31  46     mov *r1+,*r0+   ; move words
0217 6042 0642  14     dect r2         ; count down
0218 6044 16FD  14     jne SFLP2
0219 6046 0603  14     dec r3          ; count down pages
0220 6048 16F6  14     jne SFLP
0221               CODEST
0222 604A 0460  28     b @START        ; jump to startup code in RAM
     604C A980     
0223               
0224               ; fixed program in high RAM - magic bank number higher than normally legal
0225               ; this will be chopped up and inserted into the first three banks
0226               ; we're still in bank 0 - this will result in a gap in the output binary
0227               ; that we can use to put the pieces together more easily.
0228                   aorg >a000

0232               ; Write register to VDP - R0 = reg in MSB, data in LSB
0233               WRTVDP
0234 A000 0260  22     ori r0,>8000
     A002 8000

     A008 4000

     A014 8C02

0250               ; Write byte to VDP - address in R0, data in MSB R2
0251               ; Inline address set to avoid needing to cache r11
0252               WRTVRM
0253 A018 0260  22     ori r0,>4000
     A01A 4000     
0254 A01C 06C0  14     swpb r0
0255 A01E D800  30     movb r0,@VDPWADR
     A020 8C02     
0256 A022 06C0  14     swpb r0
0257 A024 D800  30     movb r0,@VDPWADR
     A026 8C02     
0258               ; No need to delay after setting a write address - there's no VRAM access
0259 A028 D802  30     movb r2,@VDPWDATA
     A02A 8C00     
0260 A02C 045B  20     b *r11
0261               
0262               ; Read byte from VDP - address in R0, data returned in MSB R0
0263               ; Inline address set to avoid needing to cache r11
0264               RDVRM
0265 A02E 06C0  14     swpb r0
0266 A030 D800  30     movb r0,@VDPWADR
     A032 8C02     
0267 A034 06C0  14     swpb r0
0268 A036 D800  30     movb r0,@VDPWADR
     A038 8C02     
0269 A03A 1000  14     nop
0270 A03C D020  30     movb @VDPDATA,r0
     A03E 8800     
0271 A040 045B  20     b *r11
0272               
0273               ; Fill VRAM - address in R0, byte in R2, count in R3
0274               ; Original: address in pointer, byte in temp, count in temp2 (ZP)
0275               ; Inline address set to avoid needing to cache r11
0276               FILVRM
0277 A042 0260  22     ori r0,>4000
     A044 4000     
0278 A046 06C0  14     swpb r0
0279 A048 D800  30     movb r0,@VDPWADR
     A04A 8C02     
0280 A04C 06C0  14     swpb r0
0281 A04E D800  30     movb r0,@VDPWADR
     A050 8C02     
0282               ; No need to delay after setting a write address - there's no VRAM access
0283               !1
0284 A052 D802  30     movb r2,@VDPWDATA
     A054 8C00     
0285 A056 0603  14     dec r3
0286 A058 16FC  14     jne -!1
0287 A05A 045B  20     b *r11
0288               
0289               ; Read VRAM - address in R0, CPU data at R2, count in R3
0290               ; Inline address set to avoid needing to cache r11
0291               LDIRMV
0292 A05C 06C0  14     swpb r0
0293 A05E D800  30     movb r0,@VDPWADR
     A060 8C02

     A066 8C02

0319               
0320               ; Define a pattern three times with 2k offsets - used for bitmap color and pattern tables
0321               ; Load VRAM 3 times with offset - address in R0, CPU data at R2, count in R3
0322               ; Original: address in pointer, CPU address at temp, count in temp2
0323               LDIRVM3
0324 A090 C10B  18     mov r11,r4      ; save return address
0325 A092 C142  18     mov r2,r5       ; save CPU address
0326 A094 C1C3  18     mov r3,r7       ; save count
0327 A096 06A0  32     bl @LDIRVM
     A098 A076     
0328 A09A 0220  22     ai r0,>0800     ; the OR'd mask doesn't matter
     A09C 0800     
0329 A09E C085  18     mov r5,r2       ; restore CPU
0330 A0A0 C0C7  18     mov r7,r3       ; restore count
0331 A0A2 06A0  32     bl @LDIRVM
     A0A4 A076     
0332 A0A6 0220  22     ai r0,>0800     ; the OR'd mask doesn't matter
     A0A8 0800     
0333 A0AA C085  18     mov r5,r2
0334 A0AC C0C7  18     mov r7,r3
0335 A0AE C2C4  18     mov r4,r11      ; for tail recursion
0336 A0B0 10E2  14     jmp LDIRVM
0337               
0338               ; Disable screen by setting VDP register 1 to >a2
0339               DISSCR
0340 A0B2 0300  22     limi 0
     A0B4 0000

     A0B8 81A2     
0342               DISSCR2

     A0C4 8C02

     A0C8 0002

0349

     A0CE 0000

     A0D2 81E2

0355               
0356               ; copy a set of blocks of data to VDP, offset by 32 bytes each
0357               ; address in R8, CPU data at R9, count per row in R6 (MSB), number rows in R4 (MSB), CPU stride in R5 (MSB) (VDP stride fixed at 32)
0358               ; original: address in pointer, CPU address at temp, count per row in temp2, num rows in temp2+1, stride in YYXX
0359               CPYBLK
0360 A0D6 C1CB  18     mov r11,r7      ; save return
0361 A0D8 0986  32     srl r6,8
0362 A0DA 0984  32     srl r4,8
0363 A0DC 0985  32     srl r5,8        ; bytes to words
0364 A0DE 0300  22     limi 0
     A0E0 0000     
0365               !1
0366 A0E2 C008  18     mov r8,r0       ; get vdp address
0367 A0E4 C089  18     mov r9,r2       ; get cpu address
0368 A0E6 C0C6  18     mov r6,r3       ; get count
0369 A0E8 06A0  32     bl @LDIRVM      ; copy one row
     A0EA A076     
0370 A0EC A245  18     a r5,r9         ; add stride to CPU address
0371 A0EE 0228  22     ai r8,32        ; add 32 to VDP
     A0F0 0020     
0372 A0F2 0604  14     dec r4          ; count down rows
0373 A0F4 16F6  14     jne -!1         ; loop till done
0374 A0F6 0300  22     limi 2
     A0F8 0002     
0375 A0FA 0457  20     b *r7           ; back to caller
0376               
0377               ; clear screen and reset cursor to >1800
0378               cls
0379 A0FC C10B  18     mov r11,r4      ; save return
0380 A0FE 0200  20     li r0,>1800     ; SIT address
     A100 1800     
0381 A102 C800  30     mov r0,@cursor  ; save cursor
     A104 8342     
0382 A106 0202  20     li r2,>2000     ; byte to write
     A108 2000     
0383 A10A 0203  20     li r3,768       ; number of bytes
     A10C 0300     
0384 A10E 0300  22     limi 0          ; ints off
     A110 0000     
0385 A112 06A0  32     bl @FILVRM      ; write them
     A114 A042     
0386 A116 0300  22     limi 2          ; ints back on
     A118 0002     
0387 A11A 0454  20     b *r4           ; back to caller

0390               ; CPU address in R2, length in R3
0391               print_string
0392 A11C C10B  18     mov r11,r4      ; save return
0393 A11E C020  30     mov @cursor,r0  ; get cursor pos
     A120 8342     
0394 A122 0240  22     andi r0,>07ff   ; enforce position - pretty large range though? 80 column support maybe?
     A124 07FF     
0395 A126 0220  22     ai r0,>1800     ; add is safer than OR, and we have that option
     A128 1800     
0396 A12A A803  30     a r3,@cursor    ; add the count to cursor (might as well do it now!)
     A12C 8342     
0397 A12E 0300  22     limi 0
     A130 0000     
0398 A132 06A0  32     bl @LDIRVM      ; do the write
     A134 A076     
0399 A136 0300  22     limi 2
     A138 0002     
0400 A13A 0454  20     b *r4           ; back to caller

0469               
0470               ; Load sprite definitions: Sprite number in R4, CPU data in R0, count of sprites in R5 (MSB)
0471               ; Original: pointer = sprite number, temp = CPU address, a = number sprites
0472               ; Note: sprites are all expected to be double-size 16x16, 32 bytes each, so sprite char 1 is character 4
0473               ; Sprite pattern table at >3800
0474               define_sprite
0475 A1DA C20B  18     mov r11,r8          ; save return
0476 A1DC C080  18     mov r0,r2           ; Source data.
0477 A1DE C004  18     mov r4,r0           ; VRAM target.
0478 A1E0 0A50  26     sla r0,5            ; sprite number times 32 for bytes
0479 A1E2 0220  22     ai r0,>3800         ; add VDP base
     A1E4 3800     
0480 A1E6 C0C5  18     mov r5,r3		; Length.
0481 A1E8 0983  32     srl r3,8            ; make int
0482 A1EA 0A53  26     sla r3,5            ; count times 32
0483 A1EC 0300  22     limi 0              ; ints off
     A1EE 0000     
0484 A1F0 06A0  32     bl @LDIRVM          ; do the copy
     A1F2 A076     
0485 A1F4 0300  22     limi 2              ; ints on
     A1F6 0002     
0486 A1F8 0458  20     b *r8               ; back to caller
0487               
0488               ; Load character definitions: Char number in R1, CPU data in R2, count in R3 (MSB)
0489               ; Original: pointer = char number, temp = CPU address, a = number chars
0490               ; Note this loads the pattern three times if in bitmap mode (MODE&0x04)
0491               ; Pattern table at >0000
0492               define_char
0493 A1FA C20B  18     mov r11,r8          ; save return
0494 A1FC C080  18     mov r0,r2           ; source data
0495 A1FE C004  18     mov r4,r0           ; move input to scratch
0496 A200 0A30  22     sla r0,3            ; char number times 8 (VDP base is 0, so already there)
0497 A202 C0C5  18     mov r5,r3
0498 A204 0983  32     srl r3,8            ; make word
0499 A206 0A33  22     sla r3,3            ; count times 8
0500 A208 D160  30     movb @mode,r5       ; get mode flags
     A20A 834E     
0501 A20C 0245  22     andi r5,>0800
     A20E 0800     
0502 A210 1607  14     jne !1              ; not in bitmap mode, do a single copy
0503               
0504 A212 0300  22     limi 0              ; ints off
     A214 0000     
0505 A216 06A0  32     bl @LDIRVM3         ; do the triple copy
     A218 A090     
0506 A21A 0300  22     limi 2              ; ints on
     A21C 0002     
0507 A21E 0458  20     b *r8               ; back to caller
0508               
0509               !1
0510 A220 0300  22     limi 0              ; ints off
     A222 0000     
0511 A224 06A0  32     bl @LDIRVM          ; do the single copy
     A226 A076     
0512 A228 0300  22     limi 2              ; ints on
     A22A 0002     
0513 A22C 0458  20     b *r8               ; back to caller
0514               
0515               ; Load bitmap color definitions: Char number in R1, CPU data in R2, count in R3 (MSB)
0516               ; Original: pointer = char number, temp = CPU address, a = number chars
0517               ; Note: always does the triple copy. Color table at >2000
0518               define_color
0519 A22E C20B  18     mov r11,r8          ; save return
0520 A230 C080  18     mov r0,r2           ; source data
0521 A232 C004  18     mov r4,r0           ; move input to scratch
0522 A234 0A30  22     sla r0,3            ; char number times 8
0523 A236 0220  22     ai r0,>2000         ; add base address
     A238 2000     
0524 A23A C0C5  18     mov r5,r3
0525 A23C 0983  32     srl r3,8            ; make word
0526 A23E 0A33  22     sla r3,3            ; count times 8
0527 A240 0300  22     limi 0              ; ints off
     A242 0000     
0528 A244 06A0  32     bl @LDIRVM3         ; do the triple copy
     A246 A090     
0529 A248 0300  22     limi 2              ; ints on
     A24A 0002     
0530 A24C 0458  20     b *r8               ; back to caller
0531               
0532               ; Update sprite entry - copy data (4 bytes) to sprite table mirror at sprites
0533               ; R4 = sprite number, R5 = byte 1, r6 = byte 2, r7 = byte 3, r0 = byte 4 (all MSB)
0534               ; Original: A = sprite number, source data at sprite_data
0535               update_sprite
0536 A24E 0984  32     srl r4,8            ; make word
0537 A250 0A24  20     sla r4,2            ; x4 for address
0538 A252 0224  22     ai r4,sprites       ; sprite mirror address
     A254 2000     
0539 A256 DD05  32     movb r5,*r4+        ; move bytes
0540 A258 DD06  32     movb r6,*r4+        ; move bytes
0541 A25A DD07  32     movb r7,*r4+        ; move bytes
0542 A25C DD00  32     movb r0,*r4+        ; move bytes
0543 A25E 045B  20     b *r11
0544               
0545               ; SGN R0 - return 1, -1 or 0 as 16 bit
0546               _sgn16
0547 A260 C000  18     mov r0,r0       ; check for zero
0548 A262 1306  14     jeq !1          ; if yes, we're done
0549 A264 0240  22     andi r0,>8000   ; check for negative
     A266 8000     
0550 A268 1302  14     jeq !2          ; was not
0551 A26A 0700  14     seto r0         ; was negative, make it -1
0552 A26C 045B  20     b *r11          ; back to caller
0553               !2
0554 A26E 0580  14     inc r0          ; we know it was zero, and we want 1
0555               !1
0556 A270 045B  20     b *r11          ; back to caller
0557               
0558               ; 16-bit signed modulo. R1 % R2 = R0 - 9900 doesn't do signed divide
0559               ; original was stack%stack=YYAA
0560               ; Remainder is negative if the dividend was negative
0561               _mod16s
0562 A272 04C0  14     clr r0          ; make dividend 32-bit
0563 A274 C082  18     mov r2,r2       ; check divisor for zero
0564 A276 130A  14     jeq !1
0565 A278 0742  18     abs r2          ; make sure divisor is positive
0566 A27A C041  18     mov r1,r1       ; check sign of dividend
0567 A27C 1505  14     jgt !2          ; go do the faster positive version
0568               
0569 A27E 0741  18     abs r1          ; was negative, make it positive
0570 A280 3C02 128     div r2,r0       ; do the division => r2=quotient, r3=remainder
0571 A282 0501  14     neg r1          ; make remainder negative
0572 A284 C001  18     mov r1,r0       ; into r0
0573 A286 045B  20     b *r11
0574               
0575               !2
0576 A288 3C02 128     div r2,r0       ; do the division => r2=quotient, r3=remainder
0577 A28A C001  18     mov r1,r0       ; into r0
0578               !1
0579 A28C 045B  20     b *r11
0580               
0581               ; 16-bit signed divide. R1 / R2 = R0 - 9900 doesn't do signed divide
0582               ; original was stack/stack=YYAA
0583               ; Remainder is negative if the signs differ
0584               _div16s
0585 A28E 04C0  14     clr r0          ; make dividend 32-bit
0586 A290 C0C2  18     mov r2,r3       ; check divisor for zero
0587 A292 1308  14     jeq !1          ;
0588 A294 28C1  18     xor r1,r3
0589 A296 0742  18     abs r2
0590 A298 0741  18     abs r1          ; might as well make them positive now that we have copies
0591 A29A 3C02 128     div r2,r0       ; do the divide => r0=quotient, r1=remainder
0592 A29C 0243  22     andi r3,>8000   ; mask out sign bit
     A29E 8000     
0593 A2A0 1301  14     jeq !1          ; skip ahead to positive version
0594               
0595 A2A2 0500  14     neg r0          ; negate the result
0596               !1
0597 A2A4 045B  20     b *r11
0598               
0599               ; Random number generator - return in R0, (complex one uses R3,R4, simpler one only R0)
0600               ; Original output into YYAA
0601               random
0628               ; simpler one from dreamcast days...
0629 A2A6 C020  30     mov @lfsr,r0        ; get seed
     A2A8 834C     
0630 A2AA 0910  18     srl r0,1            ; shift
0631 A2AC 1702  14     jnc .rand1          ; jump if no 1
0632 A2AE 2820  34     xor @rmask,r0       ; xor new bits
     A2B0 A2B8     
0633               .rand1
0634 A2B2 C800  30     mov r0,@lfsr        ; save the output
     A2B4 834C     
0635 A2B6 045B  20     b *r11
0636               rmask
0637 A2B8 B400         data >b400          ; mask for 16 bit
0639               
0640               ; Set SN Frequency: R0=frequency code, R2=channel command (MSB)
0641               ; Original: A=least significant byte  X=channel command  Y=most significant byte
0642               sn76489_freq
0643 A2BA C0C0  18     mov r0,r3
0644 A2BC 0243  22     andi r3,>000f
     A2BE 000F     
0645 A2C0 06C3  14     swpb r3
0646 A2C2 F083  18     socb r3,r2
0647 A2C4 D802  30     movb r2,@SOUND  ; cmd and least significant nibble
     A2C6 8400     
0648 A2C8 0940  24     srl r0,4
0649 A2CA 0240  22     andi r0,>003f
     A2CC 003F     
0650 A2CE 06C0  14     swpb r0
0651 A2D0 D800  30     movb r0,@SOUND  ; most significant byte
     A2D2 8400     
0652 A2D4 045B  20     b *r11
0653               
0654               ; Set SN volume: R0=volume (MSB, inverse of attenuation), R2=channel command (MSB)
0655               ; Original: A=volume (inverse of attenuation), X=channel command
0656               sn76489_vol
0657 A2D6 0540  14     inv r0
0658 A2D8 0240  22     andi r0,>0f00
     A2DA 0F00     
0659 A2DC F002  18     socb r2,r0
0660 A2DE D800  30     movb r0,@SOUND
     A2E0 8400     
0661 A2E2 045B  20     b *r11
0662               
0663               ; Set noise type: R0=Noise type (MSB)
0664               ; original: A=noise command
0665               sn76489_control
0666 A2E4 0240  22     andi r0,>0f00
     A2E6 0F00     
0667 A2E8 0260  22     ori r0,>e000
     A2EA E000     
0668 A2EC D800  30     movb r0,@SOUND
     A2EE 8400     
0669 A2F0 045B  20     b *r11
0670               
0671               ; Set up vdp generic settings - R0 should be preloaded with a register in MSB, data in LSB
0672               ; R2 should contain the color table entry (in MSB), R3 the bitmap table (in MSB). Rest is
0673               ; hard coded. WARNING: Disables interrupts but does not re-enable them.
0674               vdp_generic_mode
0675 A2F2 C10B  18     mov r11,r4      ; save return
0676 A2F4 0300  22     limi 0          ; ints off
     A2F6 0000     
0677               
0678 A2F8 06A0  32     bl @WRTVDP      ; caller must set up this one
     A2FA A000     
0679 A2FC 0200  20     li r0,>01a2     ; VDP mode, screen off
     A2FE 01A2     
0680 A300 06A0  32     bl @WRTVDP
     A302 A000     
0681 A304 0200  20     li r0,>0206     ; >1800 pattern table
     A306 0206     
0682 A308 06A0  32     bl @WRTVDP
     A30A A000     
0683 A30C 0200  20     li r0,>0003     ; for color table
     A30E 0003     
0684 A310 F002  18     socb r2,r0
0685 A312 06C0  14     swpb r0
0686 A314 06A0  32     bl @WRTVDP
     A316 A000     
0687 A318 0200  20     li r0,>0004     ; for pattern table
     A31A 0004     
0688 A31C F003  18     socb r3,r0
0689 A31E 06C0  14     swpb r0
0690 A320 06A0  32     bl @WRTVDP
     A322 A000     
0691 A324 0200  20     li r0,>0536     ; >1b00 for sprite attribute table
     A326 0536     
0692 A328 06A0  32     bl @WRTVDP
     A32A A000     
0693 A32C 0200  20     li r0,>0607     ; >3800 for sprite pattern table
     A32E 0607     
0694 A330 06A0  32     bl @WRTVDP
     A332 A000     
0695 A334 0200  20     li r0,>0701     ; default screen color
     A336 0701     
0696 A338 06A0  32     bl @WRTVDP
     A33A A000     
0697 A33C 0454  20     b *r4
0698               
0699               ; set up VDP mode 0
0700               mode_0
0701 A33E C20B  18     mov r11,r8      ; careful - we call vdp_generic_mode and LDIRVM3
0702 A340 0200  20     li r0,>0800     ; bit we want to clear
     A342 0800     
0703 A344 5800  30     szcb r0,@mode
     A346 834E     
0704               
0705 A348 0202  20     li r2,>ff00	    ; $2000 for color table.
     A34A FF00     
0706 A34C 0203  20     li r3,>0300	    ; $0000 for bitmaps
     A34E 0300     
0707 A350 0200  20     li r0,>0002     ; r0 setting
     A352 0002     
0708 A354 06A0  32     bl @vdp_generic_mode    ; interrupts are now off
     A356 A2F2     
0709               
0710 A358 0200  20     li r0,>0100     ; target in VDP memory
     A35A 0100     
0711 A35C 0202  20     li r2,font_bitmaps  ; CPU memory source
     A35E A674     
0712 A360 0203  20     li r3,>0300     ; number of bytes
     A362 0300     
0713 A364 06A0  32     bl @LDIRVM3
     A366 A090     
0714               
0715 A368 0300  22     limi 2
     A36A 0002     
0716 A36C 0300  22     limi 0
     A36E 0000     
0717               
0718 A370 0200  20     li r0,>2000
     A372 2000     
0719 A374 0202  20     li r2,>f000
     A376 F000     
0720 A378 0203  20     li r3,>1800     ; fill color table with white on transparent
     A37A 1800     
0721 A37C 06A0  32     bl @FILVRM
     A37E A042     
0722               
0723 A380 0300  22     limi 2
     A382 0002     
0724 A384 06A0  32     bl @cls
     A386 A0FC     
0725 A388 C2C8  18     mov r8,r11      ; restore return address, and fall through to vdp_generic_sprites
0726               
0727               ; Initialize sprite table
0728               vdp_generic_sprites
0729 A38A C20B  18     mov r11,r8      ; save return address
0730 A38C 0200  20     li r0,>1b00     ; sprite attribute table in VDP
     A38E 1B00     
0731 A390 0202  20     li r2,>d100     ; off screen, and otherwise unimportant
     A392 D100     
0732 A394 0203  20     li r3,128       ; number of bytes
     A396 0080     
0733               
0734 A398 0300  22     limi 0
     A39A 0000     
0735 A39C 06A0  32     bl @FILVRM
     A39E A042     
0736               
0737 A3A0 0200  20     li r0,sprites
     A3A2 2000     
0738 A3A4 0202  20     li r2,>d1d1     ; write 2 bytes at a time
     A3A6 D1D1     
0739 A3A8 0203  20     li r3,128
     A3AA 0080     
0740               !1
0741 A3AC CC02  34     mov r2,*r0+     ; initialize CPU mirror
0742 A3AE 0643  14     dect r3
0743 A3B0 16FD  14     jne -!1
0744               
0745 A3B2 0200  20     li r0,>01e2     ; screen on
     A3B4 01E2     
0746 A3B6 06A0  32     bl @WRTVDP
     A3B8 A000     
0747               
0748 A3BA 0300  22     limi 2
     A3BC 0002     
0749 A3BE 0458  20     b *r8
0750               
0751               ; set up VDP mode 1
0752               mode_1
0753 A3C0 C20B  18     mov r11,r8      ; careful - we call vdp_generic_mode and LDIRVM3
0754 A3C2 0200  20     li r0,>0800     ; bit we want to clear
     A3C4 0800     
0755 A3C6 5800  30     szcb r0,@mode
     A3C8 834E     
0756               
0757 A3CA 0202  20     li r2,>ff00	    ; $2000 for color table.
     A3CC FF00     
0758 A3CE 0203  20     li r3,>0300	    ; $0000 for bitmaps
     A3D0 0300     
0759 A3D2 0200  20     li r0,>0002     ; r0 setting
     A3D4 0002     
0760 A3D6 06A0  32     bl @vdp_generic_mode    ; interrupts are now off
     A3D8 A2F2     
0761               
0762 A3DA 0200  20     li r0,>0000
     A3DC 0000     
0763 A3DE 0202  20     li r2,>0000
     A3E0 0000     
0764 A3E2 0203  20     li r3,>1800
     A3E4 1800     
0765 A3E6 06A0  32     bl @FILVRM      ; clear pattern table
     A3E8 A042     
0766               
0767 A3EA 0300  22     limi 2
     A3EC 0002     
0768               
0769 A3EE 0200  20     li r0,>2000
     A3F0 2000     
0770 A3F2 0202  20     li r2,>f000
     A3F4 F000     
0771 A3F6 0203  20     li r3,>1800
     A3F8 1800     
0772               
0773 A3FA 0300  22     limi 0
     A3FC 0000     
0774 A3FE 06A0  32     bl @FILVRM      ; init color table
     A400 A042     
0775 A402 0300  22     limi 2
     A404 0002     
0776               
0777 A406 0200  20     li r0,>5800     ; >1800 with the write bit set
     A408 5800     
0778 A40A 04C3  14     clr r3          ; value to write
0779               
0780               !1
0781 A40C 0300  22     limi 0          ; write the screen image table, but pause every 32 bytes for interrupts
     A40E 0000     
0782               
0783 A410 06C0  14     swpb r0
0784 A412 D800  30     movb r0,@VDPWADR
     A414 8C02     
0785 A416 06C0  14     swpb r0
0786 A418 D800  30     movb r0,@VDPWADR
     A41A 8C02     
0787               
0788 A41C 0202  20     li r2,32
     A41E 0020     
0789               
0790               !2
0791 A420 D803  30     movb r3,@VDPWDATA
     A422 8C00     
0792 A424 0223  22     ai r3,>0100
     A426 0100     
0793 A428 0602  14     dec r2
0794 A42A 16FA  14     jne -!2
0795               
0796 A42C 0300  22     limi 2
     A42E 0002     
0797 A430 0220  22     ai r0,32
     A432 0020     
0798 A434 0280  22     ci r0,>5b00
     A436 5B00     
0799 A438 1AE9  14     jl -!1
0800               
0801 A43A C2C8  18     mov r8,r11      ; restore return address
0802 A43C 10A6  14     jmp vdp_generic_sprites     ; using tail recursion
0803               
0804               ; Set up VDP mode 2
0805               mode_2
0806 A43E C20B  18     mov r11,r8      ; careful - we call vdp_generic_mode and LDIRVM3
0807 A440 0200  20     li r0,>0800     ; bit we want to set
     A442 0800     
0808 A444 F800  30     socb r0,@mode
     A446 834E     
0809               
0810 A448 0202  20     li r2,>8000	    ; $2000 for color table.
     A44A 8000

     A44E 0000

     A452 0000

     A456 A2F2     
0814

     A45A 0100

     A45E A674

     A462 0300

     A466 A076     
0819               
0820 A468 0300  22     limi 2
     A46A 0002     
0821 A46C 0300  22     limi 0
     A46E 0000     
0822               
0823 A470 0200  20     li r0,>2000
     A472 2000     
0824 A474 0202  20     li r2,>f000
     A476 F000     
0825 A478 0203  20     li r3,>0020
     A47A 0020

     A47E A042     
0827               
0828 A480 0300  22     limi 2
     A482 0002

     A486 A0FC     
0830 A488 C2C8  18     mov r8,r11      ; restore return
0831 A48A 0460  28     b @vdp_generic_sprites
     A48C A38A     
0832               
0833               ; this is where interrupts happen every frame
0834               ; Unlike a normal TI application, this one runs with interrupts ON,
0835               ; so all operations need to be sure to protect VDP address with LIMI 0,
0836               ; as well as any operations that might need to manipulate data managed
0837               ; by this interrupt. We enter via the normal user hook, so WP is on
0838               ; GPLWS, interrupts are off, and the VDP is already reset and status
0839               ; stashed on vdp_status (>837b). Our return address to the ROM is in
0840               ; r11, but we are NOT going to use it so that we don't need to reserve
0841               ; r8 for whatever nonsense it does. That means we need to load intws
0842               ; and RTWP ourselves at the end. We are on our own workspace so we
0843               ; don't have to worry about the main app's workspace.
0844               int_handler
0845               ; first copy the sprite table
0846 A48E 02E0  18     lwpi myintwp        ; separate safe workspace
     A490 8320     
0847               
0851               
0852 A492 020B  20     li r11,>005b        ; >1b00 with the write bit added, and byte flipped
     A494 005B     
0853 A496 D80B  30     movb r11,@VDPWADR   ; SAL address
     A498 8C02     
0854 A49A 06CB  14     swpb r11
0855 A49C D80B  30     movb r11,@VDPWADR   ; going to copy the sprite table to VDP
     A49E 8C02     
0856               
0857 A4A0 D2E0  30     movb @mode,r11
     A4A2 834E     
0858 A4A4 024B  22     andi r11,>0400      ; if bit >04 (inhibit flicker) is cleared, jump ahead to rotate
     A4A6 0400     
0859 A4A8 130A  14     jeq !4
0860               
0861 A4AA 04CB  14     clr r11             ; else we're going to just write it straight across
0862 A4AC 020C  20     li r12,128
     A4AE 0080     
0863 A4B0 020D  20     li r13,sprites
     A4B2 2000     
0864               !7
0865 A4B4 D83D  40     movb *r13+,@VDPWDATA
     A4B6 8C00     
0866 A4B8 060C  14     dec r12
0867 A4BA 16FC  14     jne -!7
0868 A4BC 101B  14     jmp !5
0869               
0870               !4
0871 A4BE D2E0  30     movb @flicker,r11   ; here we write it rotated every frame
     A4C0 834F     
0872 A4C2 022B  22     ai r11,>0400
     A4C4 0400     
0873 A4C6 024B  22     andi r11,>7f00
     A4C8 7F00     
0874 A4CA D80B  30     movb r11,@flicker
     A4CC 834F     
0875 A4CE 06CB  14     swpb r11            ; make count
0876 A4D0 020C  20     li r12,32           ; count
     A4D2 0020     
0877               
0878               !6
0879 A4D4 022B  22     ai r11,sprites        ; this is still faster than separate incs
     A4D6 2000     
0880 A4D8 D83B  40     movb *r11+,@VDPWDATA  ; copy one sprite
     A4DA 8C00     
0881 A4DC D83B  40     movb *r11+,@VDPWDATA  ; no delay needed
     A4DE 8C00     
0882 A4E0 D83B  40     movb *r11+,@VDPWDATA
     A4E2 8C00     
0883 A4E4 D81B  38     movb *r11,@VDPWDATA   ; small optimization, since we have an add coming anyway
     A4E6 8C00     
0884 A4E8 022B  22     ai r11,-(sprites-1)   ; remove address and add the rest of the increment
     A4EA E001     
0885 A4EC 024B  22     andi r11,>007F        ; clamp it in range
     A4EE 007F     
0886 A4F0 060C  14     dec r12
0887 A4F2 16F0  14     jne -!6
0888               !5
0889               
0890               ; next read the joysticks - output needs to be 21xxLDRU - 1 and 2 are button and button2 respectively
0891               ; We don't have a button 2. We also need to read the keyboard and fill in key1_data. key2_data we
0892               ; will leave unused. Note key1_data expects Coleco-style 0-9,10-*,11-#,15=not pressed, but we can throw
0893               ; everything else as ASCII. We could do a split keyboard for 2 players, but I guess we'll leave it for now.
0894               ; joy1
0895 A4F4 020C  20     li r12,>0024    ; CRU base of select output
     A4F6 0024     
0896 A4F8 020D  20     li r13,>0600    ; joystick 1 column
     A4FA 0600     
0897 A4FC 30CD  30     ldcr r13,3      ; select it
0898 A4FE 0B7C  30     src r12,7       ; delay
0899 A500 020C  20     li r12,>0006    ; CRU base of return read
     A502 0006     
0900 A504 360D  48     stcr r13,8      ; read 8 bits (we could get away with fewer, but be consistent)
0901 A506 06A0  32     bl @convert_joystick
     A508 A5C8     
0902 A50A D80C  30     movb r12,@joy1_data
     A50C 8346     
0903               
0904               ; joy2
0905 A50E 020C  20     li r12,>0024    ; CRU base of select output
     A510 0024     
0906 A512 020D  20     li r13,>0700    ; joystick 2 column
     A514 0700     
0907 A516 30CD  30     ldcr r13,3      ; select it
0908 A518 0B7C  30     src r12,7       ; delay
0909 A51A 020C  20     li r12,>0006    ; CRU base of return read
     A51C 0006     
0910 A51E 360D  48     stcr r13,8      ; read 8 bits (we could get away with fewer, but be consistent)
0911 A520 06A0  32     bl @convert_joystick
     A522 A5C8     
0912 A524 D80C  30     movb r12,@joy2_data
     A526 8347     
0913               
0914               ; do a quick modifier read for button 2 (control and fctn for joy 1 and 2 respectively)
0915 A528 020C  20     li r12,>0024    ; CRU base of select output
     A52A 0024     
0916 A52C 04CD  14     clr r13         ; modifiers
0917 A52E 30CD  30     ldcr r13,3      ; select it
0918 A530 0B7C  30     src r12,7       ; delay
0919 A532 020C  20     li r12,>0006    ; CRU base of return read
     A534 0006     
0920 A536 360D  48     stcr r13,8      ; read 8 bits (we could get away with fewer, but be consistent)
0921 A538 020C  20     li r12,>4000    ; control
     A53A 4000     
0922 A53C 020B  20     li r11,>8000    ; button 2 bit
     A53E 8000     
0923 A540 274C  18     czc r12,r13
0924 A542 1602  14     jne .noc1b2
0925 A544 F80B  30     socb r11,@joy1_data
     A546 8346     
0926               .noc1b2
0927 A548 020C  20     li r12,>1000    ; fctn
     A54A 1000     
0928 A54C 274C  18     czc r12,r13
0929 A54E 1602  14     jne .noc2b2
0930 A550 F80B  30     socb r11,@joy2_data
     A552 8347     
0931               .noc2b2
0932               
0933               ; key1 - this is a very simple read with no modifiers, it just gives access to the letters and numbers
0934 A554 04CB  14     clr r11         ; column
0935               !key1
0936 A556 020C  20     li r12,>0024    ; CRU base of select output
     A558 0024     
0937 A55A 30CB  30     ldcr r11,3      ; select column
0938 A55C 0B7C  30     src r12,7       ; delay
0939 A55E 020C  20     li r12,>0006    ; CRU base of return read
     A560 0006     
0940 A562 360D  48     stcr r13,8      ; get the bits
0941 A564 020C  20     li r12,7        ; bit search
     A566 0007     
0942               !key2
0943 A568 0A1C  18     sla r12,1
0944 A56A 276C  34     czc @masktable(r12),r13    ; bit set?
     A56C A638     
0945 A56E 1607  14     jne !key3       ; continue
0946 A570 091C  18     srl r12,1
0947 A572 095B  26     srl r11,5
0948 A574 A2CC  18     a r12,r11       ; calculate table offset
0949 A576 D82B  46     movb @keyboard_table(r11),@key1_data    ; might be a dead key, but that's okay
     A578 A608     
     A57A 8348     
0950 A57C 100D  14     jmp !key4
0951               
0952               !key3
0953 A57E 091C  18     srl r12,1
0954 A580 060C  14     dec r12
0955 A582 15F2  14     jgt -!key2
0956 A584 13F1  14     jeq -!key2      ; we don't have a jump if not negative
0957               
0958 A586 022B  22     ai r11,>0100
     A588 0100     
0959 A58A 028B  22     ci r11,>0600
     A58C 0600     
0960 A58E 16E3  14     jne -!key1
0961               
0962 A590 020B  20     li r11,>0f00
     A592 0F00     
0963 A594 D80B  30     movb r11,@key1_data     ; no key was pressed
     A596 8348     
0964               !key4
0965               
0966               ; check for quit - attempts to work it into the above were not working
0967               ; borrowed from console ROM
0968 A598 020C  20     li r12,>0024
     A59A 0024     
0969 A59C 30CC  30     ldcr r12,3
0970 A59E 0B7C  30     src r12,7
0971 A5A0 020C  20     li r12,>0006
     A5A2 0006     
0972 A5A4 360B  48     stcr r11,8
0973 A5A6 020C  20     li r12,>1100
     A5A8 1100     
0974 A5AA 26CC  18     czc r12,r11
0975 A5AC 1604  14     jne .noquit
0976 A5AE 04E0  26     clr @intwsr2
     A5B0 83C4     
0977 A5B2 0420  42     blwp @>0000
     A5B4 0000     
0978               .noquit
0979               
0986               
0987 A5B6 05A0  26     inc @frame
     A5B8 834A     
0988 A5BA 0200  20     li r0,3
     A5BC 0003     
0989 A5BE A800  30     a r0,@lfsr  ; Make LFSR more random
     A5C0 834C     
0990               
1006               
1007               
1008               ; restore the saved bank
1013               
1014               ; get back the interrupt workspace and return
1015 A5C2 02E0  18     lwpi INTWS
     A5C4 83C0     
1016 A5C6 0380  18     RTWP
1017               
1018               ; given a joystick read in r13, return bits in r12
1019               ; The final output is 8 bits:
1020               ; 21xxLDRU - 1 and 2 are button and button2 respectively
1021               ; NOTE: if called by the compiler, this won't act as expected
1022               convert_joystick
1023 A5C8 04CC  14     clr r12
1024 A5CA 2760  34     czc @joystick_table,r13
     A5CC A5FE     
1025 A5CE 1602  14     jne !j1
1026 A5D0 026C  22     ori r12,>0800
     A5D2 0800     
1027               !j1
1028 A5D4 2760  34     czc @joystick_table+2,r13
     A5D6 A600     
1029 A5D8 1602  14     jne !j2
1030 A5DA 026C  22     ori r12,>0400
     A5DC 0400     
1031               !j2
1032 A5DE 2760  34     czc @joystick_table+4,r13
     A5E0 A602     
1033 A5E2 1602  14     jne !j3
1034 A5E4 026C  22     ori r12,>0200
     A5E6 0200     
1035               !j3
1036 A5E8 2760  34     czc @joystick_table+6,r13
     A5EA A604     
1037 A5EC 1602  14     jne !j4
1038 A5EE 026C  22     ori r12,>0100
     A5F0 0100     
1039               !j4
1040 A5F2 2760  34     czc @joystick_table+8,r13
     A5F4 A606     
1041 A5F6 1602  14     jne !j5
1042 A5F8 026C  22     ori r12,>4000
     A5FA 4000     
1043               !j5
1044 A5FC 045B  20     b *r11
1045               
1046               joystick_table
1047 A5FE 0200         data >0200,>0800,>0400,>1000,>0100    ; LDRU1
     A600 0800     
     A602 0400     
     A604 1000     
     A606 0100     
1048               
1049               ; By columns, then rows. 8 Rows per column. No shift states - converted to the Coleco returns
1050               ; for numbers, , and . become ; and #. Control is control1 button2, and Fctn is control2 button2
1051               keyboard_table
1052 A608 3D20         byte 61,32,11,15,254,15,255,15  ; '=',' ',enter,n/a,fctn,shift,ctrl,n/a
     A60A 0B0F     
     A60C FE0F     
     A60E FF0F     
1053 A610 2E4C         byte 46,76,79,9,2,83,87,88      ; '.','L','O','9','2','S','W','X'
     A612 4F09     
     A614 0253     
     A616 5758     
1054 A618 2C4B         byte 44,75,73,8,3,68,69,67      ; ',','K','I','8','3','D','E','C'
     A61A 4908     
     A61C 0344     
     A61E 4543     
1055 A620 4D4A         byte 77,74,85,7,4,70,82,86      ; 'M','J','U','7','4','F','R','V'
     A622 5507     
     A624 0446     
     A626 5256     
1056 A628 4E48         byte 78,72,89,6,5,71,84,66      ; 'N','H','Y','6','5','G','T','B'
     A62A 5906     
     A62C 0547     
     A62E 5442     
1057 A630 0A3B         byte 10,59,80,0,1,65,81,90      ; '/',';','P','0','1','A','Q','Z'
     A632 5000     
     A634 0141     
     A636 515A     
1058               
1059               masktable
1060 A638 0100         data >0100,>0200,>0400,>0800,>1000,>2000,>4000,>8000
     A63A 0200     
     A63C 0400     
     A63E 0800     
     A640 1000     
     A642 2000     
     A644 4000     
     A646 8000     
1061 A648 0F00         data >0f00
1062               
1063               ; wait for frame to increment
1064               wait
1065 A64A C020  30     mov @frame,r0
     A64C 834A     
1066               !1
1067 A64E 8800  30     c r0,@frame
     A650 834A     
1068 A652 13FD  14     jeq -!1
1069 A654 045B  20     b *r11
1070               
1071               ; initialize music system
1072               music_init
1073               ; mute sound chip
1074 A656 0200  20     li r0,>9fbf
     A658 9FBF     
1075 A65A D800  30     movb r0,@SOUND
     A65C 8400     
1076 A65E 06C0  14     swpb r0
1077 A660 D800  30     movb r0,@SOUND
     A662 8400     
1078 A664 0200  20     li r0,>dfff
     A666 DFFF     
1079 A668 D800  30     movb r0,@SOUND
     A66A 8400     
1080 A66C 06C0  14     swpb r0
1081 A66E D800  30     movb r0,@SOUND
     A670 8400     
1082               
1084               ; return if we don't have the player compiled in
1085 A672 045B  20     b *r11

1928               
1929               ; The stack is simulated using R10. It's not used in
1930               ; these functions but the compiled code will need it.
1931               ; To push: dect r10, mov r0,*r10
1932               ; To pop:  mov *r10+,r0
1933               ; However, for JSR a function is helpful - call this like:
1934               ; bl @jsr
1935               ; data <function_address>
1936               jsr
1937 A974 C3BB  30     mov *r11+,r14       ; get the jump address
1938 A976 064A  14     dect r10            ; make room on stack
1939 A978 C68B  30     mov r11,*r10        ; save return address
1940 A97A 069E  24     bl *r14             ; new subroutine call, we can come back here
1941 A97C C2FA  30     mov *r10+,r11       ; get real return off stack - warning, all basic functions do this inline rather than return
1942 A97E 045B  20     b *r11              ; back to caller
1943               
1944               ; entry code - we should enter with ints off anyway
1945               START
1946 A980 0300  22     limi 0
     A982 0000     
1947 A984 02E0  18     lwpi mywp           ; get our private workspace
     A986 8300     
1948 A988 020A  20     li R10,>4000        ; pseudo stack pointer
     A98A 4000     
1949 A98C D820  42     movb @>8802,@vdp_status  ; clear any pending VDP interrupt and initialize vdp_status if needed
     A98E 8802     
     A990 837B

     A994 0182

     A998 A000

1984               ;;; CVBasic code starts here
1985               	; 	' ============================================================
1986               	; 	' ADVENTIRE - an Atari-2600-Adventure-style action-adventure.
1987               	; 	' Original code, art, and room data throughout (a mechanics
1988               	; 	' homage: layouts and connections are our own adaptation of
1989               	; 	' the game structure documented in published maps/guides).
1990               	; 	'
1991               	; 	' FOUR game variations, chosen on the title screen:
1992               	; 	'   GAME 1  INTRO KINGDOM  - our original 13-room map: a
1993               	; 	'           gentle introduction (3 castles, 3 dragons, bat,
1994               	; 	'           bridge + sealed chamber).
1995               	; 	'   GAME 2  SMALL KINGDOM  - compact kingdom in the spirit of
1996               	; 	'           the cartridge's first game: gold + black castles,
1997               	; 	'           two dragons, no bat, no dark rooms.
1998               	; 	'   GAME 3  FULL KINGDOM   - the big map: 3 castles, corridor
1999               	; 	'           row, blue maze, DARK catacombs and black-castle
2000               	; 	'           maze (fog of war), red maze, magnet, bat, and the
2001               	; 	'           hidden-dot secret room.
2002               	; 	'   GAME 4  RANDOM KINGDOM - the full kingdom with object
2003               	; 	'           locations scrambled each game.
2004               	; 	'
2005               	; 	' Core rules (all games):
2006               	; 	'  - Rooms are 32x24 grids of 8x8-pixel cells (4 bytes/row,
2007               	; 	'    authored as readable BITMAP art); collision is a RAM bit
2008               	; 	'    test, zero per-frame VRAM reads. Thin 8px walls give the
2009               	; 	'    kingdom's mazes their winding, original-cartridge look.
2010               	; 	'  - Dragons ignore walls entirely and PURSUE you from room
2011               	; 	'    to room (a live dragon you escape bursts in ~1.3s later).
2012               	; 	'  - Doorways whose exit leads nowhere in the selected game
2013               	; 	'    are sealed on entry, so collision and visuals agree.
2014               	; 	'  - Carry ONE object (touch = pick up / swap, FIRE = drop);
2015               	; 	'    a carried object keeps the offset where you grabbed it.
2016               	; 	'  - Keys open the matching castle gate on touch; walk up into
2017               	; 	'    the open archway to enter.
2018               	; 	'  - The SWORD slays dragons on contact, carried or lying.
2019               	; 	'  - The BRIDGE: grab by its RAILS, drop across a wall (snaps
2020               	; 	'    to the block grid) and walk through its dark channel.
2021               	; 	'  - The MAGNET (games 3/4) drags every loose object in its
2022               	; 	'    room toward it - even out of sealed chambers.
2023               	; 	'  - The BAT steals objects, even from your hands.
2024               	; 	'  - DARK rooms (games 3/4) reveal walls only near you.
2025               	; 	'  - The invisible DOT (games 3/4) hides in the black castle
2026               	; 	'    maze chamber; bring it + 2 objects to the corridor's east
2027               	; 	'    end and the wall opens to a secret room.
2028               	; 	'  - Swallowed or victorious -> back to the title (game
2029               	; 	'    select); every start is a full reset.
2030               	; 	'
2031               	; 	' Build (ONE source, dual target):
2032               	; 	'   TI-99/4A:     cvbasic --ti994a adventire.bas -> xas99 -> linkticart
2033               	; 	'   ColecoVision: cvbasic adventire.bas -> gasm80 -> adventire.rom
2034               	; 	' Loop is paced to 30Hz (two WAITs) on both machines.
2035               	; 	' ============================================================
2036               	;
2037               	; 	' rooms are 32x24 grids of 8x8-pixel cells ("quarter blocks"):
2038               	; 	' 4 bytes per row x 24 rows = 96 bytes, MSB = leftmost cell
2039               	; 	DIM rm(96), msk(8)
2040               	; 	DIM orm(8), obx(8), oby(8), ocl(8)
2041               	; 	DIM drm(3), ddx(3), ddy(3), dst(3), dcl(3), dsp(3), gop(3), fdl(3)
2042               	;
2043               	; 	BORDER 1
2044 A9EE 0200  20 	li r0,256   ; 1*256
     A9F0 0100     
2045 A9F2 0980  32 	srl r0,8

     A9F6 8700

     A9FC 0000

     AA00 8C02

     AA06 8C02
